# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

61-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive analysis of the etcd-io/etcd client-side retry and timeout policy implementation. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've identified **9 key Go source files** that implement the client-side retry and timeout policy in etcd-io/etcd:

### Core Components:

1. **gRPC Retry Interceptor** (`client/v3/retry_interceptor.go`)
   - Implements unary and stream client interceptors
   - Configurable max retries (default 100 for unary, disabled for streams)
   - Exponential backoff with jitter (25ms base, 10% jitter)
   - Auth token refresh on authentication errors

2. **Endpoint Balancer** (`client/v3/internal/resolver/resolver.go`)
   - Round-robin load balancing across endpoints
   - Dynamic endpoint updates via `SetEndpoints()`
   - Automatic failover to healthy endpoints

3. **Connection Health Check** (`client/v3/client.go`)
   - gRPC Health Checking Protocol integration
   - Enforces timeout for connection establishment
   - Validates endpoint responsiveness before use

4. **Retry Policy Classification** (`client/v3/retry.go`)
   - `isSafeRetryImmutableRPC`: For read operations (Get, Lease queries)
   - `isSafeRetryMutableRPC`: For write operations with write-at-most-once semantics (Put, Delete)
   - Specialized retry clients for KV, Lease, Cluster, Maintenance, and Auth operations

5. **Request Timeout Enforcement** (multiple files)
   - **KV Operations**: Direct timeout via context passing
   - **Watch Operations**: Internal stream with reconnection, respects user context cancellation
   - **Lease Operations**: Initial keepalive timeout + dynamic deadline management
   - **Context Error Conversion**: Proper timeout/cancellation reporting via `ContextError()`

\"clientv3/retry_interceptor: cannot retry on ClientStreams, set Disable()\")\n131: \t\t}\n132: \t\tnewStreamer, err := streamer(ctx, desc, cc, method, grpcOpts...)\n133: \t\tif err != nil {\n134: value.\n152: func (c *Client) shouldRefreshToken(err error, callOpts *options) bool {\n153: \tif c.Token != \"\" {\n154: \t\t// do not try to refresh the token as it is set by user\n155: \t\treturn refreshToken(ctx context.Context) error {\n169: \tif c.authTokenBundle == nil {\n170: \t\t// c.authTokenBundle will be initialized only when\n171: \t\t// c.Username != \"\" && c.Password != \"\".\n172: \t\t//\n173: \t\t// When users use the TLS CommonName based authentication, the\n174: \t\t// authTokenBundle is always nil. But it's possible for the clients\n175: \t\t// to get `rpctypes.ErrAuthOldRevision` response when the clients\n176: \t\t// concurrently modify auth data (e.g, addUser, deleteUser etc.).\n177: \t\t// In this case, there is no need to refresh the token; instead the\n178: \t\t// clients just need to retry the operations (e.g. Put, Delete etc).\n179: \t\treturn nil\n180: \t}\n181: \n182: \treturn c.getToken(ctx)\n183: }\n184: \n185: // type serverStreamingRetryingStream is the implementation of grpc.ClientStream that acts as a\n186: // proxy to the underlying call. If any of the RecvMsg() calls fail, it will try to reestablish\n187: // a new ClientStream according to the retry policy.\n188: type serverStreamingRetryingStream struct {\n189: \t\"google.golang.org/grpc\"\n22: \t\"google.golang.org/grpc/codes\"\n23: \t\"google.golang.org/grpc/status\"\n24: \n25: \tpb \"go.etcd.io/etcd/api/v3/etcdserverpb\"\n26: \t\"go.etcd.io/etcd/api/v3/v3rpc/rpctypes\"\n27: )\n28: \n29: type retryPolicy uint8\n30: \n31: const (\n32: \trepeatable retryPolicy = iota\n33: \tnonRepeatable\n34: )\n35: \n36: func (rp retryPolicy) String() string {\n37: \tswitch rp {\n38: \tcase repeatable:\n39: \t\treturn \"repeatable\"\n40: \tcase nonRepeatable:\n41: \t\treturn \"nonRepeatable\"\n42: \tdefault:\n43: \t\treturn \"UNKNOWN\"\n44: \t}\n45: }\n46: \n47: // isSafeRetryImmutableRPC returns \"true\" when an immutable request is safe for retry.\n48: //\n49: // immutable requests (e.g. Get) should be retried unless it's\n50: // an obvious server-side error (e.g. rpctypes.ErrRequestTooLarge).\n51: //\n52: // Returning \"false\" means retry should stop, since client cannot\n53: // handle itself even with retries.\n54: func isSafeRetryImmutableRPC(err error) bool {\n55: \teErr := rpctypes.Error(err)\n56: \tvar serverErr rpctypes.EtcdError\n57: \tif errors.As(eErr, &serverErr) && serverErr.Code() != codes.Unavailable {\n58: \t\t// interrupted by non-transient server-side or gRPC-side error\n59: \t\t// client cannot handle itself (e.g. rpctypes.ErrCompacted)\n60: \t\treturn false\n61: \t}\n62: \t// only retry if unavailable\n63: \tev, ok := status.FromError(err)\n64: \tif !ok {\n65: \t\t// all errors from RPC is typed \"grpc/status.(*statusError)\"\n66: \t\t// (ref. https://github.com/grpc/grpc-go/pull/1782)\n67: \t\t//\n68: \t\t// if the error type is not \"grpc/status.(*statusError)\",\n69: \t\t// it could be from \"Dial\"\n70: \t\t// TODO: do not retry for now\n71: \t\t// ref. https://github.com/grpc/grpc-go/issues/1581\n72: \t\treturn false\n73: \t}\n74: \treturn ev.Code() == codes.Unavailable\n75: }\n76: \n77: // isSafeRetryMutableRPC returns \"true\" when a mutable request is safe for retry.\n78: //\n79: // mutable requests (e.g. Put, Delete, Txn) should only be retried\n80: // when the status code is codes.Unavailable when initial connection\n81: // has not been established (no endpoint is up).\n82: //\n83: // Returning \"false\" means retry should stop, otherwise it violates\n84: // write-at-most-once semantics.\n85: func isSafeRetryMutableRPC(err error) bool {\n86: \tif ev, ok := status.FromError(err); ok && ev.Code() != codes.Unavailable {\n87: \t\t// not safe for mutable RPCs\n88: \t\t// e.g. interrupted by non-transient error that client cannot handle itself,\n89: \t\t// or transient error while the connection has already been established\n90: \t\treturn false\n91: \t}\n92: \tdesc := rpctypes.ErrorDesc(err)\n93: \treturn desc == \"there is no address available\" || desc == \"there is no connection available\"\n94: }\n95: \n96: type retryKVClient struct {\n97: \tkc pb.KVClient\n98: implements a sophisticated client-side retry and timeout policy through multiple coordinated components:\\n\\n## Retry Interceptor\\nThe primary retry mechanism is implemented in `client/v3/retry_interceptor.go`, which provides:\\n- `unaryClientInterceptor`: Handles retries for unary (non-streaming) gRPC calls with configurable max retries (default 100), exponential backoff with jitter (25ms base, 10% jitter), and special handling for auth token refresh on ErrInvalidAuthToken and ErrAuthOldRevision errors.\\n- `streamClientInterceptor`: Handles retries for server-side streaming calls (Watch operations), buffering messages and re-establishing streams on recoverable errors.\\n- `serverStreamingRetryingStream`: A gRPC stream wrapper that buffers sent messages and retries receiving operations while preserving the original client stream interface.\\n- `waitRetryBackoff`: Manages backoff timing between retry attempts with context-aware deadline handling.\\n- `isSafeRetry`: Determines retry safety based on error type and retry policy (repeatable for immutable ops, non-repeatable for mutable ops).\\n\\n## Retry Policy Classification\\nThe `client/v3/retry.go` file defines fine-grained retry policies:\\n- `isSafeRetryImmutableRPC`: Allows retries for immutable operations (Get, Lease queries) on Unavailable status codes, stopping on other server errors.\\n- `isSafeRetryMutableRPC`: Restricts retries for mutable operations (Put, Delete) to only when no endpoint is available (write-at-most-once semantics).\\n- Provides specialized retry clients: `RetryKVClient`, `RetryLeaseClient`, `RetryClusterClient`, `RetryMaintenanceClient`, `RetryAuthClient` that apply the appropriate policy to each operation.\\n\\n## Endpoint Balancer and Health Check\\nThe endpoint balancer is implemented in `client/v3/internal/resolver/resolver.go`:\\n- `EtcdManualResolver`: A gRPC resolver that maintains a list of endpoints with round-robin load balancing policy (configured via service config).\\n- Updates endpoints dynamically via `SetEndpoints()` and distributes requests across active endpoints.\\n- The `Build()` method configures round-robin load balancing with automatic failover.\\n\\nConnection health checking occurs in `client/v3/client.go`:\\n- `waitForConnection`: Performs gRPC health checks (using gRPC Health Checking Protocol) before considering a connection ready, verifying the endpoint is responsive.\\n- Uses `DialTimeout` configuration to bound the health check duration.\\n- Gracefully handles Unimplemented and FailedPrecondition responses from servers not supporting health checks.\\n\\n## Request Timeout Enforcement\\nTimeout handling is integrated across multiple layers:\\n\\n1. **Dial Timeout** (`client/v3/client.go`):\\n   - `dialSetupOpts`: Configures the gRPC client with the retry interceptors and timeout policies during connection setup.\\n   - `newClient`: Applies DialTimeout (default behavior calls `waitForConnection` with DialTimeout context).\\n   - Enforces timeout for initial connection establishment.\\n\\n2. **KV Operations** (`client/v3/kv.go`):\\n   - `NewKV`: Creates KV client wrapping `RetryKVClient` with the client's call options.\\n   - `Put`, `Get`, `Delete`, `Do`: All pass context through to gRPC calls, which enforce caller-provided context timeouts via `context.WithTimeout()`.\\n   - Errors are processed through `ContextError()` to convert context deadline exceeded errors appropriately.\\n\\n3. **Watch Operations** (`client/v3/watch.go`):\\n   - `NewWatcher`: Creates watch client with call options from the parent client.\\n   - `Watch`: Establishes a `watchGRPCStream` that maintains internal stream context with `context.WithCancel()` (never closes on user timeout, allowing reconnection).\\n   - Uses special `valCtx` context that never expires internally but respects user context cancellation for shutdown.\\n\\n4. **Lease Operations** (`client/v3/lease.go`):\\n   - `NewLease`: Creates lease client with `firstKeepAliveTimeout` set to `DialTimeout + 1 second` for initial keepalive deadline.\\n   - `Grant`, `Revoke`, `TimeToLive`, `Leases`: Pass context directly to `RetryLeaseClient` calls.\\n   - `KeepAlive`: Runs indefinite loop handling keep-alive messages with dynamic deadline tracking.\\n   - `KeepAliveOnce`: Renews lease with caller-provided context timeout.\\n\\n5. **Context Error Conversion** (`client/v3/client.go`):\\n   - `ContextError()`: Converts gRPC DeadlineExceeded and Canceled errors to the underlying context error if the context has actually expired/canceled, enabling proper timeout semantics.\\n   - Used by all KV, Watch, and Lease operations to report accurate timeout/cancellation information.\\n\\n## Configuration\\nTimeout and retry behavior is configured through:\\n- `client/v3/config.go`: Defines `Config` struct with `DialTimeout`, `MaxUnaryRetries`, `BackoffWaitBetween`, `BackoffJitterFraction` fields.\\n- `client/v3/options.go`: Defines defaults (`defaultUnaryMaxRetries = 100`, `defaultBackoffWaitBetween = 25ms`, `defaultBackoffJitterFraction = 0.10`).\\n- `client/v3/client.go`: Applies these settings during client initialization in `dialSetupOpts()` via the retry interceptor configuration.\\n\\n## Backoff Strategy\\nThe `roundRobinQuorumBackoff()` in `client/v3/client.go` implements intelligent backoff:\\n- Calculates backoff duration based on endpoint count and quorum size.\\n- Ensures retries are distributed across the cluster endpoints to improve recovery speed.\\n- Uses linear backoff with jitter to prevent thundering herd during cluster recovery.\\n\\nThis comprehensive architecture ensures reliable client-server communication through coordinated retry logic, health checking, endpoint balancing, and proper timeout enforcement across all operation types (KV, Watch, Lease).\"\n}\n",

context error if the context has actually expired/canceled, enabling proper timeout semantics.\\n   - Used by all KV, Watch, and Lease operations to report accurate timeout/cancellation `BackoffJitterFraction` fields.\\n- `client/v3/options.go`: Defines defaults (`defaultUnaryMaxRetries = 100`, `defaultBackoffWaitBetween = 25ms`, `defaultBackoffJitterFraction = 0.10`).\\n- `client/v3/client.go`: Applies these settings during client initialization in `dialSetupOpts()` via the retry interceptor configuration.\\n\\n## Backoff Strategy\\nThe `roundRobinQuorumBackoff()` in `client/v3/client.go` implements intelligent backoff:\\n- Calculates backoff duration based on endpoint count and quorum size.\\n- Ensures retries are distributed across the cluster endpoints to improve recovery speed.\\n- Uses linear backoff with jitter to prevent thundering herd during cluster recovery.\\n\\nThis comprehensive architecture ensures reliable client-server communication through coordinated retry logic, health checking, endpoint balancing, and proper timeout enforcement across all operation types (KV, Watch, Lease).\"\n}\n",
